## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) governs the reaction dynamics, where the functional form reveals the reaction order and mechanism.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law from reversible or parallel reactions)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction with conservation constraint)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order)
- Consecutive reaction with time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (coupled sequential reactions after elimination)
- Parallel competing reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (linearly varying external influence)
- Exponential catalyst decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reaction with decaying catalyst activity)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or complex mechanism)
- Square-root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (dissociative mechanism or surface reaction)
- Combined mechanism: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → standard rate law dA/dt = f(A), indicating elementary or pseudo-elementary reaction
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system suggesting time-varying external conditions (light, temperature ramp, catalyst deactivation)
- Integer power of A → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power
- Fractional power of A → complex mechanism involving pre-equilibrium or surface adsorption steps
- Rational function of A (polynomial/polynomial) → enzyme-like saturation kinetics or Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface mechanism
- Product A*(c-A) form → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics with conservation of total concentration
- Sign of leading coefficient → negative indicates consumption (reactant), positive indicates production (product)
- Multiple additive power-law terms → parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms operating simultaneously
- Rate proportional to exp(c*t)*A → coupled system where an intermediate follows exponential dynamics affecting A
